This is often cited as a serious threat to his professional and personal reputation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> His closest partner <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Roux" title="Émile Roux">Émile Roux</a>, who had medical qualifications, refused to participate in the <a href="/wiki/Clinical_trial" title="Clinical trial">clinical trial</a>, likely because he considered it unjust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_126-4"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-126">[126]</a></sup> However, Pasteur executed vaccination of the boy under the close watch of practising physicians <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Joseph_Grancher" title="Jacques-Joseph Grancher">Jacques-Joseph Grancher</a>, head of the Paris Children's Hospital's paediatric clinic, and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Vulpian" title="Alfred Vulpian">Alfred Vulpian</a>, a member of the Commission on Rabies. He was not allowed to hold the syringe, although the inoculations were entirely under his supervision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wasik_125-3"><a href="#cite_note-Wasik-125">[125]</a></sup> It was Grancher who was responsible for the injections, and he defended Pasteur before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_de_M%C3%A9decine" title="Académie de Médecine">French National Academy of Medicine</a> in the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>Pasteur has also been criticized for keeping secrecy of his procedure and not giving proper pre-clinical trials on animals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ligon_7-9"><a href="#cite_note-Ligon-7">[7]</a></sup> Pasteur stated that he kept his procedure secret in order to control its quality. He later disclosed his procedures to a small group of scientists. Pasteur wrote that he had successfully vaccinated 50 rabid dogs before using it on Meister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> According to Geison, Pasteur's laboratory notebooks show that he had vaccinated only 11 dogs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ligon_7-10"><a href="#cite_note-Ligon-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>Meister never showed any symptoms of rabies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jackson_126-5"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-126">[126]</a></sup> but the vaccination has not been proved to be the reason. One source estimates the probability of Meister contracting rabies at 10%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Giese_114-2"><a href="#cite_note-Giese-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span></h2>
<p>Pasteur was awarded 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Franc" title="Franc">francs</a> in 1853 by the Pharmaceutical Society for the synthesis of <a href="/wiki/Racemic_acid" title="Racemic acid">racemic acid</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> In 1856 the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> of London presented him the <a href="/wiki/Rumford_Medal" title="Rumford Medal">Rumford Medal</a> for his discovery of the nature of racemic acid and its relations to polarized light,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Copley_Medal" title="Copley Medal">Copley Medal</a> in 1874 for his work on fermentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> He was elected a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Fellows_of_the_Royal_Society_elected_in_1869" title="List of Fellows of the Royal Society elected in 1869">Foreign Member of the Royal Society (ForMemRS) in 1869</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-formemrs_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-formemrs-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_Academy_of_Sciences" title="French Academy of Sciences">French Academy of Sciences</a> awarded Pasteur the 1859 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montyon_Prizes" title="Montyon Prizes">Montyon Prize</a> for experimental physiology in 1860,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Debré_&amp;_Patrice_pp._505-7_44-2"><a href="#cite_note-Debré_&amp;_Patrice_pp._505-7-44">[44]</a></sup> and the Jecker Prize in 1861 and the Alhumbert Prize in 1862 for his experimental refutation of spontaneous generation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-porter_77-3"><a href="#cite_note-porter-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Though he lost elections in 1857 and 1861 for membership to the French Academy of Sciences, he won the 1862 election for membership to the mineralogy section.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> He was elected to permanent secretary of the physical science section of the academy in 1887 and held the position until 1889.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1873, Pasteur was elected to the <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_Nationale_de_M%C3%A9decine" title="Académie Nationale de Médecine">Académie Nationale de Médecine</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> and was made the commander in the Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Rose" title="Order of the Rose">Order of the Rose</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> In 1881 he was elected to a seat at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A9mie_fran%C3%A7aise" title="Académie française">Académie française</a> left vacant by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Littr%C3%A9" title="Émile Littré">Émile Littré</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Pasteur received the <a href="/wiki/Albert_Medal_(Royal_Society_of_Arts)" title="Albert Medal (Royal Society of Arts)">Albert Medal</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Arts" title="Royal Society of Arts">Royal Society of Arts</a> in 1882.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frankland_&amp;_Frankland_p._211_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frankland_&amp;_Frankland_p._211-168">[168]</a></sup> In 1883 he became foreign member of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences">Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> In 1885, he was elected as a member to the <a href="/wiki/American_Philosophical_Society" title="American Philosophical Society">American Philosophical Society</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> On 8 June 1886, the Ottoman Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hamid_II" title="Abdul Hamid II">Abdul Hamid II</a> awarded Pasteur with the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Medjidie" title="Order of the Medjidie">Order of the Medjidie</a> (I Class) and 10000 Ottoman liras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> He was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Prize_for_Therapeutics_of_the_University_of_Edinburgh" title="Cameron Prize for Therapeutics of the University of Edinburgh">Cameron Prize for Therapeutics of the University of Edinburgh</a> in 1889.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Pasteur won the <a href="/wiki/Leeuwenhoek_Medal" title="Leeuwenhoek Medal">Leeuwenhoek Medal</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences">Royal Netherlands Academy of Arts and Sciences</a> for his contributions to <a href="/wiki/Microbiology" title="Microbiology">microbiology</a> in 1895.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>Pasteur was made a Chevalier of the <a href="/wiki/Legion_of_Honour" title="Legion of Honour">Legion of Honour</a> in 1853, promoted to Officer in 1863, to Commander in 1868, to Grand Officer in 1878 and made a Grand Cross of the Legion of Honor in 1881.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frankland_&amp;_Frankland_p._211_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-Frankland_&amp;_Frankland_p._211-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg/220px-Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg/330px-Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg/440px-Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Danang_Vietnam_rue_Pasteur2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pasteur Street (<i>Đường Pasteur</i>) in <a href="/wiki/Da_Nang" title="Da Nang">Da Nang</a>, Vietnam.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG"><img alt="Pasteur's street in Odessa." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG/220px-Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG/330px-Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG/440px-Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vulitsya_Pastera.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vulitsya Pastera or Pasteur Street in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_things_named_after_Louis_Pasteur" title="List of things named after Louis Pasteur">List of things named after Louis Pasteur</a></div>
<p>In many localities worldwide, streets are named in his honor. For example, in the US: <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irvine,_California" title="Irvine, California">Irvine, California</a>, Boston and Polk, Florida, adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_Health_Science_Center_at_San_Antonio" title="University of Texas Health Science Center at San Antonio">University of Texas Health Science Center at San Antonio</a>; Jonquière, Québec; San Salvador de Jujuy and Buenos Aires (<a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>), <a href="/wiki/Great_Yarmouth" title="Great Yarmouth">Great Yarmouth</a> in Norfolk, in the United Kingdom, Jericho and Wulguru in Queensland, (Australia); <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Ho Chi Minh City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Da_Nang" title="Da Nang">Da Nang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>; Batna in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>; <a href="/wiki/Bandung" title="Bandung">Bandung</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tehran" title="Tehran">Tehran</a> in <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, near the central campus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warsaw_University" title="Warsaw University">Warsaw University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw" title="Warsaw">Warsaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>; adjacent to the Odessa State Medical University in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odessa" title="Odessa">Odessa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>; <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> in Italy and <a href="/wiki/Bucharest" title="Bucharest">Bucharest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cluj-Napoca" title="Cluj-Napoca">Cluj-Napoca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timi%C8%99oara" title="Timișoara">Timișoara</a> in <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>. The Avenue Pasteur in Saigon, Vietnam, is one of the few streets in that city to retain its French name. <i>Avenue Louis Pasteur</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Longwood_Medical_and_Academic_Area" title="Longwood Medical and Academic Area">Longwood Medical and Academic Area</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a> was named in his honor in the French manner with "Avenue" preceding the name of the dedicatee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p><p>Both the Institut Pasteur and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Louis_Pasteur" title="Université Louis Pasteur">Université Louis Pasteur</a> were named after Pasteur. The schools <a href="/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Pasteur_(Neuilly-sur-Seine)" title="Lycée Pasteur (Neuilly-sur-Seine)">Lycée Pasteur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Neuilly-sur-Seine" title="Neuilly-sur-Seine">Neuilly-sur-Seine</a>, France, and <a href="/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Louis_Pasteur_(Calgary)" title="Lycée Louis Pasteur (Calgary)">Lycée Louis Pasteur</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calgary" title="Calgary">Calgary, Alberta</a>, Canada, are named after him. In South Africa, the Louis Pasteur Private Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Pretoria" title="Pretoria">Pretoria</a>, and Life Louis Pasteur Private Hospital, <a href="/wiki/Bloemfontein" title="Bloemfontein">Bloemfontein</a>, are named after him. Louis Pasteur University Hospital in <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">Košice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> is also named after Pasteur.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice,_Poliklinika_(1).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Poliklinika_%281%29.JPG/220px-UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Poliklinika_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Poliklinika_%281%29.JPG/330px-UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Poliklinika_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Poliklinika_%281%29.JPG/440px-UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice%2C_Poliklinika_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UNLP_Ko%C5%A1ice,_Poliklinika_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Louis Pasteur University Hospital, <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">Košice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a></div></div></div>
<p>A statue of Pasteur is erected at <a href="/wiki/San_Rafael_High_School" title="San Rafael High School">San Rafael High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Rafael,_California" title="San Rafael, California">San Rafael, California</a>. A bronze bust of him resides on the French Campus of <a href="/wiki/Kaiser_Permanente" title="Kaiser Permanente">Kaiser Permanente</a>'s San Francisco Medical Center in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>. The sculpture was designed by Harriet G. Moore and cast in 1984 by Artworks Foundry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOS_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-SOS-176">[176]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/UNESCO/Institut_Pasteur_Medal" title="UNESCO/Institut Pasteur Medal">UNESCO/Institut Pasteur Medal</a> was created on the centenary of Pasteur's death, and is given every two years in his name, "in recognition of outstanding research contributing to a beneficial impact on human health".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco-2005_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-2005-177">[177]</a></sup>
</p><p>The french Academician <a href="/wiki/Henri_Mondor" title="Henri Mondor">Henri Mondor</a> stated: "<i>Louis Pasteur was neither a physician nor a surgeon, but no one has done as much for medicine and surgery as he has</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mondor_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mondor-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pasteur_Institute">Pasteur Institute</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pasteur_Institute" title="Pasteur Institute">Pasteur Institute</a></div>
<p>After developing the rabies vaccine, Pasteur proposed an institute for the vaccine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> In 1887, fundraising for the Pasteur Institute began, with donations from many countries. The official statute was registered in 1887, stating that the institute's purposes were "the treatment of rabies according to the method developed by M. Pasteur" and "the study of virulent and contagious diseases".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wasik_125-4"><a href="#cite_note-Wasik-125">[125]</a></sup> The institute was inaugurated on 14 November 1888.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wasik_125-5"><a href="#cite_note-Wasik-125">[125]</a></sup> He brought together scientists with various specialties. The first five departments were directed by two graduates of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_Normale_Sup%C3%A9rieure" title="École Normale Supérieure">École Normale Supérieure</a></i>: <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Duclaux" title="Émile Duclaux">Émile Duclaux</a> (general <a href="/wiki/Microbiology" title="Microbiology">microbiology</a> research) and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Chamberland" title="Charles Chamberland">Charles Chamberland</a> (microbe research applied to <a href="/wiki/Hygiene" title="Hygiene">hygiene</a>), as well as a biologist, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lie_Metchnikoff" title="Élie Metchnikoff">Élie Metchnikoff</a> (morphological microbe research) and two <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Joseph_Grancher" title="Jacques-Joseph Grancher">Jacques-Joseph Grancher</a> (<a href="/wiki/Rabies" title="Rabies">rabies</a>) and <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Roux" title="Émile Roux">Émile Roux</a> (technical microbe research). One year after the inauguration of the institute, Roux set up the first course of microbiology ever taught in the world, then entitled <i>Cours de Microbie Technique</i> (Course of microbe research techniques). Since 1891 the Pasteur Institute had been extended to different countries, and currently there are 32 institutes in 29 countries in various parts of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Pasteur_en_1857.jpg"><img alt="Louis Pasteur in 1857" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="254" decoding="async" height="333" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Louis_Pasteur_en_1857.jpg/220px-Louis_Pasteur_en_1857.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Louis_Pasteur_en_1857.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louis_Pasteur_en_1857.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pasteur in 1857</div></div></div>
<p>Pasteur married <a href="/wiki/Marie_Pasteur" title="Marie Pasteur">Marie Pasteur</a> (née Laurent) in 1849.  She was the daughter of the rector of the University of Strasbourg, and was Pasteur's scientific assistant.  They had five children together, three of whom died as children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> Their eldest daughter, Jeanne, was born in 1850. She died from <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a>, aged 9, whilst at the boarding school <a href="/wiki/Arbois" title="Arbois">Arbois</a> in 1859. In 1865, 2-year-old Camille died of a liver tumour. Shortly after they decided to bring Cécile home from boarding school, but she too died of typhoid fever on 23 May 1866 at the age of 12. Only Jean Baptiste (b. 1851) and Marie Louise (b. 1858) survived to adulthood. Jean Baptiste would be a soldier in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> between <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faith_and_spirituality">Faith and spirituality</span></h3>
<p>His grandson, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Pasteur_Vallery-Radot" title="Louis Pasteur Vallery-Radot">Louis Pasteur Vallery-Radot</a>, wrote that Pasteur had kept from his Catholic background only a spiritualism without religious practice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> However, Catholic observers often said that Pasteur remained an ardent Christian throughout his whole life, and his son-in-law wrote, in a biography of him:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Absolute faith in God and in Eternity, and a conviction that the power for good given to us in this world will be continued beyond it, were feelings which pervaded his whole life; the virtues of the gospel had ever been present to him. Full of respect for the form of religion which had been that of his forefathers, he came simply to it and naturally for spiritual help in these last weeks of his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The <i>Literary Digest</i> of 18 October 1902 gives this statement from Pasteur that he prayed while he worked:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r996844942" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Posterity will one day laugh at the foolishness of modern materialistic philosophers. The more I study nature, the more I stand amazed at the work of the Creator. I pray while I am engaged at my work in the laboratory.</p></blockquote>
<p>Maurice Vallery-Radot, grandson of the brother of the son-in-law of Pasteur and outspoken Catholic, also holds that Pasteur fundamentally remained Catholic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> According to both Pasteur Vallery-Radot and Maurice Vallery-Radot, the following well-known <a href="/wiki/Quotation" title="Quotation">quotation</a> attributed to Pasteur is apocryphal:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> "The more I know, the more nearly is my faith that of the Breton peasant. Could I but know all I would have the faith of a Breton peasant's wife".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catholic_intro_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-catholic_intro-18">[18]</a></sup> According to Maurice Vallery-Radot,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> the false quotation appeared for the first time shortly after the death of Pasteur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> However, despite his belief in God, it has been said that his views were that of a freethinker rather than a Catholic, a spiritual more than a religious man.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> He was also against mixing science with religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h3>
<p>In 1868, Pasteur suffered a severe brain stroke that paralysed the left side of his body, but he recovered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">stroke</a> or <a href="/wiki/Uremia" title="Uremia">uremia</a> in 1894 severely impaired his health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> Failing to fully recover, he died on 28 September 1895, near Paris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cohn_53-4"><a href="#cite_note-cohn-53">[53]</a></sup> He was given a <a href="/wiki/State_funeral" title="State funeral">state funeral</a> and was buried in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre Dame de Paris">Cathedral of Notre Dame</a>, but his remains were reinterred in the Pasteur Institute in Paris,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> in a vault covered in depictions of his accomplishments in <a href="/wiki/Mosaic#Byzantine_mosaics" title="Mosaic">Byzantine mosaics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Without this work that I was asked to do for the Correspondence of the Institute, I would have stayed in Strasbourg. But you understand that this leave that these missions made me have with full salary is an irregularity that needs to be covered by a health reason." (Pasteur, letter of 25 February 1854 to his father, in Pasteur, <i>Correspondance</i>, t. 1, Paris, 1940, p. 261.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pasteur, letter of 8 May 1854 to his father, in Pasteur, <i>Correspondance</i>, t. 1, Paris, 1940, p. 267. This episode in Pasteur's career is noted by Pierre-Yves Laurioz, <i>Louis Pasteur. La réalité après la légende</i>, Paris, 2003, pp. 79–81. On Pasteur's attitude towards money, see Richard Moreau, <i>La Préhistoire de Pasteur</i>, Paris, L'Harmattan, 2000, pp. 257–262.</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Gal-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Gal_52-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Joseph Gal: <i>Louis Pasteur, Language, and Molecular Chirality. I. Background and Dissymmetry</i>, Chirality <i>23</i> (<b>2011</b>) 1−16.</span>

<li id="cite_note-cohn-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-cohn_53-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cohn_53-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cohn_53-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cohn_53-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-cohn_53-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFCohn,_David_V2006">Cohn, David V (18 December 2006). <a class="external text" href="http://eri.louisville.edu/~eri/fos/interest1.html" rel="nofollow">"Pasteur"</a>. University of Louisville<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 December</span> 2007</span>. <q>Fortunately, Pasteur's colleagues Chamberlain  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] and Roux followed up the results of a research physician Jean-Joseph-Henri Toussaint, who had reported a year earlier that carbolic-acid/heated anthrax serum would immunize against anthrax. These results were difficult to reproduce and discarded although, as it turned out, Toussaint had been on the right track. This led Pasteur and his assistants to substitute an anthrax vaccine prepared by a method similar to that of Toussaint and different from what Pasteur had announced.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Pasteur&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Louisville&amp;rft.date=2006-12-18&amp;rft.au=Cohn%2C+David+V&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feri.louisville.edu%2F~eri%2Ffos%2Finterest1.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>
</li>

Retrieved <span class="nowrap">1 May</span> 2021</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Wellcome+Collection&amp;rft.atitle=M%C3%A9moire+sur+les+corpuscules+organis%C3%A9s+qui+existent+dans+l%27atmosph%C3%A8re%3A+examen+de+la+doctrine+des+g%C3%A9n%C3%A9rations+spontan%C3%A9es&amp;rft.date=1882&amp;rft.aulast=Pastuer&amp;rft.aufirst=Louis&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwellcomecollection.org%2Fworks%2Fnjdg2696&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/Template:Cite_web" title="Template:Cite web">cite web</a>}}</code>:  CS1 maint: url-status (<a href="/wiki/Category:CS1_maint:_url-status" title="Category:CS1 maint: url-status">link</a>)</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFCarter1991">Carter, K. C. (1991). <a class="external text" href="https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/1802317" rel="nofollow">"The development of Pasteur's concept of disease causation and the emergence of specific causes in nineteenth-century medicine"</a>. <i>Bulletin of the History of Medicine</i>. <b>65</b> (4): 528–548. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JSTOR_(identifier)" title="JSTOR (identifier)">JSTOR</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.jstor.org/stable/44442642" rel="nofollow">44442642</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/1802317" rel="nofollow">1802317</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Bulletin+of+the+History+of+Medicine&amp;rft.atitle=The+development+of+Pasteur%27s+concept+of+disease+causation+and+the+emergence+of+specific+causes+in+nineteenth-century+medicine&amp;rft.volume=65&amp;rft.issue=4&amp;rft.pages=528-548&amp;rft.date=1991&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.jstor.org%2Fstable%2F44442642%23id-name%3DJSTOR&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F1802317&amp;rft.aulast=Carter&amp;rft.aufirst=K.+C.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fpubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2F1802317&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-82">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Jimmy Drulhon, <i>Louis Pasteur. Five years in the Cévennes</i>, Ed. Hermann, 2009. Pasteur stayed and carried out his scientific work at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Magnanerie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Magnanerie (page does not exist)">magnanerie</a> of Pont Gisquet, on the road to Saint-Jean-du-Pin.<a class="external text" href="https://www.google.fr/maps/@44.121694,4.059807,3a,75y,179.7h,70.21t/data=!3m4!1e1!3m2!1sufDCWdKLIc2BJ7ebZ8HMrg!2e0" rel="nofollow">See Google Street.</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-83">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"He had known it [= flacherie] for a long time, since his first stay in the South in 1865, where one of the two farms that had served as a starting point departure to his deductions was affected by this disease, at the same time as that of the corpuscles." Émile Duclaux, <i>Pasteur, Histoire d'un esprit</i>, pp. 218–219, available on <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k764468/f223.table" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"This denomination of <i>white-dead</i>, used by the Abbé de Sauvages and several other writers, is inaccurate; this is why I thought it necessary to add that of <i>dead-flats</i>, vulgarly used in several departments, and which designates very well the state of softness and flaccidity in which the worms dead of this disease are found. » Pierre Hubert Nysten, <i>Research on the diseases of silkworms</i>, Paris, 1808, p. 5, available on <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.be/books?id=1tRIAAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA12" rel="nofollow">Google Books</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-85"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-85">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See account of Quatrefages reproduced in L. Pasteur, <i>Études sur la maladie des vers à soie</i>, Paris, 1870, Complete Works of Pasteur, t. 4, p. 27, <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k73599/f40.table" rel="nofollow">online</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"But the cases of association were so frequent, precisely because the disease of the corpuscles was so widespread, that Pasteur had thought that the two conditions were linked to each other and should disappear together. » (Émile Duclaux, <i>Pasteur, Histoire d'un esprit</i>, pp. 218–219, <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k764468/f223.table" rel="nofollow">online</a>.) Pasteur expressed this opinion, in particular in « Nouvelles études sur la maladie des vers à soie », Comptes rendus de l'Académie des sciences, t. 63 (1866), pp. 126–142: “I am very much inclined to believe that there is no actual actual disease of silkworms. The disease complained of seems to me to have always existed, but to a lesser degree. (...) Furthermore, I have serious grounds for believing that most of the diseases of the silkworm which have been known for a long time are linked to the one which occupies us, muscardine and, perhaps, grasserie excepted. (p. 136). Available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k30204/f136.table" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>. Same thing in a letter of June 27, 1866 to Dumas: "all the other so-called ancient diseases of the silkworm, minus the <i>muscardine</i> and perhaps the <i>grasserie</i>, such as the disease of <i> motrs -flats</i>, <i>petits</i>, <i>passis</i>, <i>arpians</i>, are only forms of the actual disease. » (Pasteur, <i>Correspondance</i>, t. 2, p. 265. Quoted by Ph. Decourt, <i>Les vérités indésirables</i>, Paris, 1989, p. 173, and by P. Pinet, <i>Pasteur et la phiolosophie</i>, Paris, 2004, p. 158.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-87">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Sur la maladie des vers à soie. Lettre de M. L. Pasteur à M. Dumas", Comptes rendus de l'Académie des sciences, meeting of 3 June 1867, t. 64, p. 1113. Available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k3021f/f1122.table" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Philippe Decourt, <i>Les vérités indésirables</i>, Paris, 1989, pp. 165–193, accuses Pasteur of a denial of justice towards Antoine Béchamp, who studied pebrine at the same time as Pasteur and immediately affirmed the parasitic nature of the disease.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-89">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Balbiani, Balbiani, « Recherches sur les corpuscules de la pébrine et sur leur mode de propagation », Comptes rendus de l'Académie des Sciences, session of 27 August 1866, vol. 63 (1866), pp. 388–391, available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k30204/f388.table" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>. Balbiani begins in this manner: "Among all the contradictory opinions which have been expressed on the nature of the corpuscles of the pébrine, the most debatable, in my opinion, is that which consists in assimilating them to anatomical elements either normal, or more or less altered., or to morbid products such as pus globules, etc. This opinion was refuted more than eight years ago by Professor Lebert (...); but I believe I can also bring, against the way of seeing cited above, more decisive proofs, based on the observation of the phenomena which these corpuscles present in their evolution, phenomena which put beyond doubt their close relationship with the parasitic organisms. known under the name of <i>Psorospermia</i>".</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"As for the opinions expressed by Mr. Balbiani on the nature of the corpuscles, although I do not share them, I will take great care to examine them, for two reasons: because they are from a skilful observer, and because I still only have preconceived views on the objects they concern, to which I do not agree more than reason. There is more: I earnestly hope that the ideas of MM. Balbiani and Leydig are true (...)". Pasteur, "Observations au sujet d'une Note de M. Balbiani relative à la maladie des vers à soie", <i>Comptes rendus de l'Académie des Sciences</i>, meeting of 10 September 1866, vol. 63 (1866), pp. 441–443.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-91">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On 29 May 1867, Pasteur wrote to Dumas again: “Despite all that I would have to say about the notes of Béchamp, Estor, Balbiani and on the articles that the first two insert in the <i>Messager du Midi</i>, I take your advice, I do not answer. If you knew how erroneous it is to say that this disease is not constitutional and only parasitic. Its essential character is precisely its constitutional character. » (Quoted by Ph. Decourt, <i>Les vérités indésirables</i>, Paris, 1989, p. 190.)</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-92">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">P. Debré, <i>Louis Pasteur</i>, Flammarion, 1994, p. 219. In his <i>Études sur la maladie des vers à soie</i> (<i>Studies on silkworm disease</i>), published in 1870 (Pasteur's Complete Works, vol. 4, available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k73599" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>), Pasteur reports that he consulted Leydig on the question of the living nature of corpuscles. (One of his letters to Leydig is from December 1866.) He admits that "in substance" he adopted the opinions of Leydig and Balbiani, but he contradicts them on the question of the mode of formation of the corpuscles (pp. 135, 137 and 138). In 1884, Balbiani will examine Pasteur's theory on the development of corpuscles and will conclude as follows: "I believe that it is useless to dwell any longer on the observations of M. Pasteur, which I think I can characterize with a single word by saying that their author proves in it how little he is familiar with the researches of biology. But with this reservation, I do justice to his work, which has rendered sericulture farmers a real service by enabling them to recognize a healthy seed from a diseased seed. » (G. Balbiani, <i>Leçons sus les sporozoaires</i>, Paris, 1884, pp. 160–163, <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/leonssurlesspo00balb" rel="nofollow">online.</a>) On Pasteur's errors in the study of silkworms and his own judgment on these errors, see Richard Moreau, “Le dernier pli cacheté de Louis Pasteur à l’Académie des sciences”, La vie des sciences, <i>Comptes rendus</i>, série générale, t. 6, 1989, n° 5, pp. 403–434, <a class="external text" href="https://www.academie-sciences.fr/archivage_site/fondations/lp_pdf/Plis_07_1869.pdf" rel="nofollow">online</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-93"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-93">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Louis Pasteur, <i>Études sur la maladie des vers à soie</i>; Œuvres complètes, t. 4, pp. 166–167, available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k73599/f195.table" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pasteur mentions Osimo's ideas in Louis Pasteur, <i>Études sur la maladie des vers à soie</i>, Œuvres complètes, t. 4, pp. 38–39, available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k73599/f57.table" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>. Summarizing a development by Émile Duclaux (Émile Duclaux, <i>Pasteur, histoire d'un esprit</i>, Sceaux, 1896, p. 198, available at <a class="external text" href="https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148" rel="nofollow">/bpt6k764468/f203.notice Gallica</a>), P. Debré wrote that Pasteur was “led to propose a seed sorting method almost identical to that recommended a few years earlier by Orcino [read: Osimo]. If the latter had failed, asserts Pasteur, it was through a lack of confidence; which, of course, is not his case. » P. Debré, <i>Louis Pasteur</i>, Flammarion, 1994, p. 210.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-95"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-95">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Patrice Debré, Louis Pasteur, Flammarion, 1995, p. 246.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Elie Reynier, <i>La soie en Vivarais</i>, 1921, <a class="external text" href="http://www.nemausensis.com/ardeche/soie/LaMaladie.htm" rel="nofollow">online</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">(<i>Comptes rendus sténographiques du Congrès international séricicole, tenu à Paris du 5 au 10 septembre 1878</i>; Paris, 1879, pp. 27–38. <i>Œuvres complètes</i> of Pasteur, t. 4, pp. 698–713, spec. 699 and 713; available on <a class="external text" href="http://gallica2.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k73599.image.f746.langEN.tableDesMatieres" rel="nofollow">Gallica</a>.</span>

<li id="cite_note-Artenstein_p._75-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Artenstein_p._75_103-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFArtenstein2009">Artenstein, Andrew W., ed. <li id="cite_note-:1-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-:1_104-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-:1_104-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-:1_104-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation journal cs1" id="CITEREFSmith2012">Smith, Kendall A. <li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"This way, which the genius of Pasteur had opened and which became so fruitful, soon proved to be closed with regard to the anti-pasteurellic vaccination of the hen. Difficulties arose in the regularity of attenuation and maintenance of virulence to a definite and fixed degree." (G. Lesbouyries, <i>La pathologie des oiseaux</i>, Paris, 1941, p. 340; quoted by Hervé Bazin, <i>L'Histoire des vaccinations</i>, John Libbey Eurotext, 2008, p. 155.)</span>

<li id="cite_note-183"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-183">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pasteur Vallery-Radot, Letter to Paul Dupuy, 1939, quoted by Hilaire Cuny, <i>Pasteur et le mystère de la vie</i>, Paris, Seghers, 1963, pp. 53–54. Patrice Pinet, <i>Pasteur et la philosophie</i>, Paris, 2005, pp. 134–135, quotes analogous assertions of Pasteur Vallery-Radot, with references to Pasteur Vallery-Radot, <i>Pasteur inconnu</i>, p. 232, and André George, <i>Pasteur</i>, Paris, 1958, p. 187. According to Maurice Vallery-Radot (<i>Pasteur</i>, 1994, p. 378), the false quotation appeared for the first time in the <i>Semaine religieuse ... du diocèse de Versailles</i>, 6 October 1895, p. 153, shortly after the death of Pasteur.</span>

<li id="cite_note-185"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-185">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFVallery-Radot1994">Vallery-Radot, Maurice (1994). <i>Pasteur</i>. Paris: Perrin. pp. 377–407.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Pasteur&amp;rft.place=Paris&amp;rft.pages=377-407&amp;rft.pub=Perrin&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.aulast=Vallery-Radot&amp;rft.aufirst=Maurice&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-189"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-189">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFJoseph_McCabe1945">Joseph McCabe (1945). <a class="external text" href="https://www.infidels.org/library/historical/joseph_mccabe/dictionary.html" rel="nofollow"><i>A Biographical Dictionary of Ancient, Medieval, and Modern Freethinkers</i></a>. Haldeman-Julius Publications<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">11 August</span> 2012</span>. <q>The anonymous Catholic author quotes as his authority the standard biography by Vallery-Radot, yet this describes Pasteur as a freethinker; and this is confirmed in the preface to the English translation by Sir W. Osler, who knew Pasteur personally. Vallery-Radot was himself a Catholic yet admits that Pasteur believed only in "an Infinite" and "hoped" for a future life. Pasteur publicly stated this himself in his Academy speech in 1822 (in V.R.). He said: "The idea of God is a form of the idea of the Infinite whether it is called Brahma, Allah, Jehova, or Jesus." The biographer says that in his last days he turned to the Church but the only "evidence" he gives is that he liked to read the life of St. Vincent de Paul, and he admits that he did not receive the sacraments at death. Relatives put rosary beads in his hands, and the Catholic Encyclopedia claims him as a Catholic in virtue of the fact and of an anonymous and inconclusive statement about him. Wheeler says in his Dictionary of Freethinkers that in his prime Pasteur was Vice-President of the British Secular (Atheist) Union; and Wheeler was the chief Secularist writer of the time. The evidence is overwhelming. Yet the Catholic scientist Sir Bertram Windle assures his readers that "no person who knows anything about him can doubt the sincerity of his attachment to the Catholic Church," and all Catholic writers use much the same scandalous language.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Biographical+Dictionary+of+Ancient%2C+Medieval%2C+and+Modern+Freethinkers&amp;rft.pub=Haldeman-Julius+Publications&amp;rft.date=1945&amp;rft.au=Joseph+McCabe&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.infidels.org%2Flibrary%2Fhistorical%2Fjoseph_mccabe%2Fdictionary.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-190"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-190">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFPatrice_Debré2000">Patrice Debré (2000). <i>Louis Pasteur</i>. JHU Press. p. 176. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-6529-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-6529-9"><bdi>978-0-8018-6529-9</bdi></a>. <q>Does this mean that Pasteur was bound to a religious ideal? His attitude was that of a believer, not of a sectarian. One of his most brilliant disciples, Elie Metchnikoff, was to attest that he spoke of religion only in general terms. In fact, Pasteur evaded the question by claiming quite simply that religion has no more place in science than science has in religion. ... A biologist more than a chemist, a spiritual more than a religious man, Pasteur was held back only by the lack of more powerful technical means and therefore had to limit himself to identifying germs and explaining their generation.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Louis+Pasteur&amp;rft.pages=176&amp;rft.pub=JHU+Press&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8018-6529-9&amp;rft.au=Patrice+Debr%C3%A9&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-191"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-191">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFDebré2000">Debré, Patrice (2000). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=RzOcl-FLw30C&amp;pg=PA368" rel="nofollow"><i>Louis Pasteur</i></a>. Translated by Forster, Elborg. JHU Press. p. 368. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-6529-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-6529-9"><bdi>978-0-8018-6529-9</bdi></a>. <q>Pasteur advocated separation of science and religion: "In each one of us there are two men, the scientist and the man of faith or of doubt. These two spheres are separate, and woe to those who want to make them encroach upon one another in the present state of our knowledge!"</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Louis+Pasteur&amp;rft.pages=368&amp;rft.pub=JHU+Press&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8018-6529-9&amp;rft.aulast=Debr%C3%A9&amp;rft.aufirst=Patrice&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DRzOcl-FLw30C%26pg%3DPA368&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-192"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-192">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFPatrice_Debré2000">Patrice Debré (2000). <i>Louis Pasteur</i>. JHU Press. p. 176. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-6529-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8018-6529-9"><bdi>978-0-8018-6529-9</bdi></a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Louis+Pasteur&amp;rft.pages=176&amp;rft.pub=JHU+Press&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8018-6529-9&amp;rft.au=Patrice+Debr%C3%A9&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ALouis+Pasteur"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-196"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-196">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFVallery-Radot1919">Vallery-Radot, René (1919). <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/in.ernet.dli.2015.173907/2015.173907.The-Life-Of-Pasteur#page/n477/mode/2up" rel="nofollow"><i>The Life of Pasteur</i></a>.
